<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-74">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Most Swahili adjectives begin with either a consonant or the vowels <i>i-</i> or <i>e-</i>, listed separately above. The few adjectives beginning with other vowels do not agree with all noun classes since some are restricted to humans. NC 1 <i>m(w)-</i> is <i>mw-</i> before <i>a</i> and <i>o,</i> and reduces to <i>m-</i> before <i>u</i>; <i>wa-</i> does not change; and <i>ki-, vi-, mi-</i> become <i>ch-, vy-, my-</i> before <i>o</i> but not before <i>u</i>: <i>mwanana, waanana</i> "gentle", <i>mwororo, waororo, myororo, chororo, vyororo</i> "mild, yielding", <i>mume, waume, kiume, viume</i> "male".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In a few verbs: <i>kwenda, kwisha</i></span>
</li>
</ol></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects_and_closely_related_languages">Dialects and closely related languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Dialects and closely related languages"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This list is based on <i>Swahili and Sabaki: a linguistic history</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Dialects"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Modern standard Swahili, written in Latin, is based on <i>Kiunguja,</i> the dialect spoken in <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_City" title="Zanzibar City">Zanzibar City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lambert10_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert10-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Swahili literature and poetry, traditionally written in <a href="/wiki/Swahili_Ajami" title="Swahili Ajami">Swahili Ajami</a>, is based on <i>Kiamu</i>, the dialect of <a href="/wiki/Lamu" title="Lamu">Lamu</a> on the Kenyan Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-Mulokozi_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mulokozi-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mutiua_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mutiua-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>But there are numerous other dialects of Swahili, some of which are mutually unintelligible, such as the following:<sup id="cite_ref-Lambert10_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert10-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_dialects">Old dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Old dialects"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Maho (2009) considers these to be distinct languages:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Kimwani" class="mw-redirect" title="Kimwani">Kimwani</a></i> is spoken in the Kerimba Islands and northern coastal Mozambique.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Bravanese_dialect" title="Bravanese dialect">Chimwiini</a></i> is spoken by the ethnic minorities in and around the town of <a href="/wiki/Barawa" title="Barawa">Barawa</a> on the southern coast of Somalia.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Kibajuni_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Kibajuni dialect">Kibajuni</a></i> is spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_people" title="Bajuni people">Bajuni</a> minority ethnic group on the coast and islands on both sides of the Somali–Kenyan border and in the <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_Islands" title="Bajuni Islands">Bajuni Islands</a> (the northern part of the Lamu archipelago) and is also called <i>Kitikuu</i> and <i>Kigunya</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Socotra_Swahili" class="mw-redirect" title="Socotra Swahili">Socotra Swahili</a> (extinct)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sidi_language" title="Sidi language">Sidi</a>, in Gujarat, India (possibly extinct)</li></ul>
<p>The rest of the dialects are divided by him<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> into two groups:
</p>
<ul><li>Mombasa–Lamu Swahili
<ul><li>Lamu
<ul><li>The dialects of the Lamu group (especially Kiamu, Kipate, Kingozi) are the linguistic base of the oldest (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1600 CE</span>) Swahili manuscripts and poems that reached us.<sup id="cite_ref-Mulokozi_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mulokozi-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> They are sometimes described as "literary" dialects but they were also used for everyday life and are still spoken today except Kingozi.</li>
<li><i>Kiamu</i><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> is spoken in and around the island of <a href="/wiki/Lamu" title="Lamu">Lamu</a> (Amu) and have an important corpus<sup id="cite_ref-SOAS_Swahili_manuscripts_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOAS_Swahili_manuscripts-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> of classical poems of the 18st and 19st centuries written in Arabic script (Kiajemi).</li>
<li><i>Kipate</i> is a local dialect of <a href="/wiki/Pate_Island" title="Pate Island">Pate Island</a>, considered<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (November 2022)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to be closest to the original dialect of Kingozi<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. It has also an important classical corpus<sup id="cite_ref-SOAS_Swahili_manuscripts_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOAS_Swahili_manuscripts-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> of poems from the 18st and 19st centuries.</li>
<li><i>Kingozi</i> is an extinct dialect spoken on the Indian Ocean coast between Lamu and Somalia and is sometimes still<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> used in poetry. It is often considered<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (November 2022)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> the source of Swahili<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Academic theories about Kingozi as an old literary dialect are conflicting. It is sometimes linked to <a href="/wiki/Fumo_Liyongo" title="Fumo Liyongo">the epics of Liongo</a>. For Sacleux,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> it's and old and "an exclusively literary, arcane dialect". It varies depending on the authors whose will to return to a pure form of the old language make them use Kigunya mainly (Kipate is a subdialect of Kigunya) and secondarily Kiamu and Kimvita. Knappert,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> on the contrary, states the existence of a literary <a href="/wiki/Koin%C3%A9_language" title="Koiné language">koine</a> in the 18th century based on the Kingozi as a prestigious and widespread dialect. The 2009 New Updated Guthrie List, a referential classification of the Bantu languages, considers kiOzi as a dialect in itself.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> It is not the ancestor language of Kiswahili but a member of the Lamu group (code G42a) with Kiamu, Kipate and Kisiu. This brief overview indicates that the state of research is fragmented and uncertain on the history of the kingozi.</li></ul></li>
<li>Mombasa
<ul><li><i>Chijomvu</i> is a subdialect of the Mombasa area.</li>
<li><i>Kimvita</i> is the major dialect of Mombasa (also known as "Mvita", which means "war", in reference<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to the many wars which were fought over it, the other major dialect alongside Kiunguja. It has an important classical corpus written in Arabic script from the 18st and 19st century.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Kingare</i> is the subdialect of the Mombasa area.</li></ul></li>
<li><i>Kimrima</i> is spoken around <a href="/wiki/Pangani" title="Pangani">Pangani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanga" title="Vanga">Vanga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam" title="Dar es Salaam">Dar es Salaam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rufiji_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Rufiji District">Rufiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mafia_Island" title="Mafia Island">Mafia Island</a>.</li>
<li><i>Kiunguja</i> is spoken in <a href="/wiki/Stone_Town" title="Stone Town">Zanzibar City</a> and environs on <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Unguja (Zanzibar) Island</a>. Kitumbatu (Pemba) dialects occupy the bulk of the island.</li>
<li>Mambrui, Malindi</li>
<li><i>Chichifundi</i>, a dialect of the southern Kenya coast.</li>
<li>Chwaka</li>
<li><i>Kivumba</i>, a dialect of the southern Kenya coast.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nosy_Be" title="Nosy Be">Nosse Be</a> (Madagascar)</li></ul></li>
<li>Pemba Swahili
<ul><li><i>Kipemba</i> is a local dialect of the <a href="/wiki/Pemba_Island" title="Pemba Island">Pemba Island</a>.</li>
<li><i>Kitumbatu</i> and <i>Kimakunduchi</i> are the countryside dialects of the island of Zanzibar. Kimakunduchi is a recent renaming of "Kihadimu"; the old name means "serf" and so is considered pejorative.</li>
<li>Makunduchi</li>
<li>Mafia, Mbwera</li>
<li>Kilwa (extinct)</li>
<li><i>Kimgao</i> used to be spoken around <a href="/wiki/Kilwa_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Kilwa District">Kilwa District</a> and to the south.</li></ul></li></ul>
<p>Maho includes the various <a href="/wiki/Comorian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Comorian language">Comorian</a> dialects as a third group. Most other authorities consider Comorian to be a <a href="/wiki/Sabaki_languages" title="Sabaki languages">Sabaki</a> language, distinct from Swahili.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_regions">Other regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Other regions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> <a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali language</a> predominates, a variant of Swahili referred to as <a href="/wiki/Bravanese_dialect" title="Bravanese dialect">Chimwiini</a> (also known as Chimbalazi) is spoken along the <a href="/wiki/Benadir" class="mw-redirect" title="Benadir">Benadir</a> coast by the <a href="/wiki/Bravanese_people" title="Bravanese people">Bravanese people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Another Swahili dialect known as <a href="/wiki/Kibajuni_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Kibajuni dialect">Kibajuni</a> also serves as the mother tongue of the <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_people" title="Bajuni people">Bajuni</a> minority ethnic group, which lives in the tiny <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_Islands" title="Bajuni Islands">Bajuni Islands</a> as well as the southern <a href="/wiki/Kismayo" title="Kismayo">Kismayo</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Godfrey_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Godfrey-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>, there are an estimated 52,000 people who speak Swahili as of 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Most are descendants of those repatriated after the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Zanzibar" title="Sultanate of Zanzibar">Sultanate of Zanzibar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-African_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-African-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Josephi_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Josephi-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pidgins_and_creoles">Pidgins and creoles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Pidgins and creoles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are Swahili-based slangs, pidgins and creoles:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kitaa_-_Dar_es_Salaam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kitaa - Dar es Salaam (page does not exist)">Kitaa - Dar es Salaam</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Engsh" title="Engsh">Engsh</a>&#160;– Cant from the rich neighbourhoods of Nairobi, Kenya</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/KiKAR" title="KiKAR">KiKAR</a>&#160;– Swahili pidgin spoken in British colonial East Africa</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kutchi-Swahili" title="Kutchi-Swahili">Kutchi-Swahili</a>&#160;– Creole derived from Kutchi and Swahili languages</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Settler_Swahili" title="Settler Swahili">Settler Swahili</a>&#160;– Swahili pidgin from Kenya and Zambia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sheng_slang" title="Sheng slang">Sheng slang</a>&#160;– Nairobi urban-based youth slang</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Swahili_poets">Swahili poets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Swahili poets"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Shaaban_bin_Robert" title="Shaaban bin Robert">Shaaban bin Robert</a> (1909–1962), Tanzanian poet, author, and essayist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Euphrase_Kezilahabi" title="Euphrase Kezilahabi">Euphrase Kezilahabi</a> (1944–2020), Tanzanian novelist, poet, and scholar</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mathias_E._Mnyampala" title="Mathias E. Mnyampala">Mathias E. Mnyampala</a> (1917–1969), Tanzanian writer, lawyer, and poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tumi_Molekane" title="Tumi Molekane">Tumi Molekane</a> (b. 1981), South African rapper and poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fadhy_Mtanga" title="Fadhy Mtanga">Fadhy Mtanga</a> (b. 1981), Tanzanian creative writer, photographer, graphic designer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Mwashinga" title="Christopher Mwashinga">Christopher Mwashinga</a> (b. 1965), Tanzanian author and poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mwana_Kupona" title="Mwana Kupona">Mwana Kupona</a> (d. <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1865</span>), Kenyan poet.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ebrahim_Hussein" title="Ebrahim Hussein">Ebrahim Hussein</a> (b. 1943) , Tanzanian playwright and poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haji_Gora_Haji" title="Haji Gora Haji">Haji Gora Haji</a> (1933-2021), Tanzanian poet</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alamin_Mazrui&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alamin Mazrui (page does not exist)">Alamin Mazrui</a> (b. 1948), Kenyan poet<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kithaka_wa_Mberia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kithaka wa Mberia (page does not exist)">Kithaka wa Mberia</a> (b. 1955), Poet<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Swahili_sayings">Swahili sayings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Swahili sayings"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:0em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Fuata</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nyuki</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ule</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asali.</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><sup id="cite_ref-Kamusi_la_Kiswahili_Fasaha_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamusi_la_Kiswahili_Fasaha-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 478">&#58;&#8202;478&#8202;</span></sup></p></div><p style="display: none;">Fuata nyuki ule asali.</p><p style="clear: left;">Follow the bee so that you may eat honey.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:0em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Baada</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ya</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">dhiki</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">faraja.</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><sup id="cite_ref-Kamusi_la_Kiswahili_Fasaha_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamusi_la_Kiswahili_Fasaha-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 477">&#58;&#8202;477&#8202;</span></sup></p></div><p style="display: none;">Baada ya dhiki faraja.</p><p style="clear: left;">There is no trouble that lasts forever.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:0em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Mgaagaa</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">na</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">upwa</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">hali</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">wali</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mkavu.</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><sup id="cite_ref-Kamusi_la_Kiswahili_Fasaha_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamusi_la_Kiswahili_Fasaha-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 482">&#58;&#8202;482&#8202;</span></sup></p></div><p style="display: none;">Mgaagaa na upwa hali wali mkavu.</p><p style="clear: left;">The one who busies himself with work will not miss a meal.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Elephants_fight_Amboseli_(7234358288)_(2).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3844" data-file-height="2563" /></a><figcaption><i><a href="/wiki/Loxodonta_africana" class="mw-redirect" title="Loxodonta africana">Loxodonta africana</a></i> elephants frolic in <a href="/wiki/Amboseli_National_Park" title="Amboseli National Park">Amboseli National Park</a>, Kenya, 2012.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Two sayings with the same literal meaning of <i>Where elephants fight, the grass is trampled</i> or figuratively speaking, when those with power fight, it is those below them who suffer:<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Wapiganapo</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tembo</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nyasi</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">huumia.</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></p></div><p style="display: none;">Wapiganapo tembo nyasi huumia.</p><p style="clear: left;">Fighting elephants damage the grass.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ndovu</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">wawili</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">wakisongana,</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ziumiazo</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ni</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nyika.</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></p></div><p style="display: none;">Ndovu wawili wakisongana, ziumiazo ni nyika.</p><p style="clear: left;">Where two elephants argue, the grassland is damaged.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:0em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Mwacha</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mila</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ni</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mtumwa.</p></div><p style="display: none;">Mwacha mila ni mtumwa.</p><p style="clear: left;">The person who abandons his culture, is a slave.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">Sample text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sample text"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Swahili<sup id="cite_ref-:2_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</th>
<th>English<sup id="cite_ref-:2_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Kifungu cha 26.</b>
<p>1) Kila mtu ana haki ya kuelimishwa. Elimu yapasa itolewe bure hasa ile ya madarasa ya chini. Elimu ya masarasa ya chini ihudhuriwe kwa lazima. Elimu ya ufundi na ustadi iwe wazi kwa wote. Na elimu ya juu iwe wazi kwa wote kwa kutegemea sifa ya mtu.
</p><p>2) Elimu itolewe kwa madhumuni ya kuendeleza barabara hali ya binadamu, na kwa shabaha ya kukuza haki za binadamu na uhuru wake wa asili. Elimu ni wajibu ikuze hali ya kueleana, kuvumiliana na ya urafiki kati ya mataifa na kati ya watu wa rangi na dini mbali-mbali.Kadhalika ni wajibu iendeleze shughuli za Umoja wa Mataifa za kudumisha amani.
</p><p>3) Ni haki ya wazazi kuchagua aina ya elimu ya kufunzwa watoto wao.
</p>
</td>
<td><b>Article 26</b>
<p>1. Everyone has the right to education. Education shall be free, at least in the elementary and fundamental stages. Elementary education shall be compulsory. Technical and professional education shall be made generally available and higher education shall be equally accessible to all on the basis of merit.
</p><p>2. Education shall be directed to the full development of the human personality and to the strengthening of respect for human rights and fundamental freedoms. It shall promote understanding, tolerance and friendship among all nations, racial or religious groups, and shall further the activities of the United Nations for the maintenance of peace.
</p><p>3. Parents have a prior right to choose the kind of education that shall be given to their children.
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
